       <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">
        Soconusco
       </a>
       region in the 19th
       <span class="nowrap">
       </span>
       century. The border between Mexico and Guatemala had been traditionally poorly guarded, due to diplomatic considerations, lack of resources and pressure from landowners who need cheap labor sources.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia46_53-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia46-53">
         [53]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The arrival of thousands of refugees from Central America stressed Mexico's relationship with Guatemala, at one point coming close to war as well as a politically destabilized Chiapas. Although Mexico is not a signatory to the UN
       <a href="/wiki/Convention_Relating_to_the_Status_of_Refugees" title="Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees">
        Convention Relating to the Status of Refugees
       </a>
       , international pressure forced the government to grant official protection to at least some of the refugees. Camps were established in Chiapas and other southern states, and mostly housed
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mayan_peoples" title="Mayan peoples">
        Mayan peoples
       </a>
       . However, most Central American refugees from that time never received any official status, estimated by church and charity groups at about half a million from
       <a href="/wiki/El_Salvador" title="El Salvador">
        El Salvador
       </a>
       alone.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia9_54-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia9-54">
         [54]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Mexican government resisted direct international intervention in the camps, but eventually relented somewhat because of finances.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia50_55-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia50-55">
         [55]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 1984, there were 92 camps with 46,000 refugees in Chiapas, concentrated in three areas, mostly near the Guatemalan border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia52_56-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia52-56">
         [56]
        </a>
       </sup>
       To make matters worse, the Guatemalan army conducted raids into camps on Mexican territories with significant casualties, terrifying the refugees and local populations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia53_57-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia53-57">
         [57]
        </a>
       </sup>
       From within Mexico, refugees faced threats by local governments who threatened to deport them, legally or not, and local paramilitary groups funded by those worried about the political situation in Central American spilling over into the state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia54_58-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia54-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The official government response was to militarize the areas around the camps, which limited international access and migration into Mexico from Central America was restricted.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia56_59-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia56-59">
         [59]
        </a>
       </sup>
       By 1990, it was estimated that there were over 200,000 Guatemalans and half a million from El Salvador, almost all peasant farmers and most under age twenty.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia45_60-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia45-60">
         [60]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       In the 1980s, the politization of the indigenous and rural populations of the state began in the 1960s and 1970s continued. In 1980, several ejido (communal land organizations) joined to form the Union of Ejidal Unions and United Peasants of Chiapas, generally called the Union of Unions, or UU. It had a membership of 12,000 families from over 180 communities. By 1988, this organization joined with other to form the ARIC-Union of Unions (ARIC-UU) and took over much of the Lacandon Jungle portion of the state.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sspeed_48-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-sspeed-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of the members of these organization were from Protestant and Evangelical sects as well as "Word of God" Catholics affiliated with the political movements of the Diocese of Chiapas. What they held in common was indigenous identity vis-à-vis the non-indigenous, using the old 19th century "caste war" word "Ladino" for them.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-higgens81_28-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-higgens81-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sspeed_48-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-sspeed-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mhidalgo108_52-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mhidalgo108-52">
         [52]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Neoliberalism_and_the_EZLN">
        Neoliberalism and the EZLN
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Neoliberalism and the EZLN">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       The adoption of
       <a href="/wiki/Neoliberalism" title="Neoliberalism">
        neoliberalism
       </a>
       by the Mexican federal government clashed with the leftist political ideals of these groups, notably as the reforms began to have negative economic effects on poor farmers, especially small-scale indigenous coffee-growers. Opposition would coalesce into the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EZLN" title="EZLN">
        Zapatista movement
       </a>
       in the 1990s.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-sspeed_48-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-sspeed-48">
         [48]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Although the Zapatista movement couched its demands and cast its role in response to contemporary issues, especially in its opposition to neoliberalism, it operates in the tradition of a long line of peasant and indigenous uprisings that have occurred in the state since the colonial era. This is reflected in its indigenous vs. Ladino character.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-higgens81_28-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-higgens81-28">
         [28]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296_61-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, the movement was an economic one as well. Although the area has extensive resources, much of the local population of the state, especially in rural areas, did not benefit from this bounty. In the 1990s, two thirds of the state's residents did not have sewage service, only a third had electricity and half did not have potable water. Over half of the schools offered education only to the third grade and most pupils dropped out by the end of first grade.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia54_58-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia54-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Grievances, strongest in the San Cristóbal and
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_Jungle" title="Lacandon Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </a>
       areas, were taken up by a small leftist guerrilla band led by a man called only "
       <a href="/wiki/Subcomandante_Marcos" title="Subcomandante Marcos">
        Subcomandante Marcos
       </a>
       ."
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett297_62-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett297-62">
         [62]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       This small band, called the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/EZLN" title="EZLN">
        Zapatista Army of National Liberation (Ejército Zapatista de Liberación Nacional, EZLN)
       </a>
       , came to the world's attention when on January 1, 1994 (the day the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/NAFTA" title="NAFTA">
        NAFTA
       </a>
       treaty went into effect) EZLN forces occupied and took over the towns of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/San_Cristobal_de_las_Casas" title="San Cristobal de las Casas">
        San Cristobal de las Casas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Margaritas,_Chiapas" title="Las Margaritas, Chiapas">
        Las Margaritas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Altamirano,_Chiapas" title="Altamirano, Chiapas">
        Altamirano
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ocosingo" title="Ocosingo">
        Ocosingo
       </a>
       and three others. They read their proclamation of revolt to the world and then laid siege to a nearby military base, capturing weapons and releasing many prisoners from the jails.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-hisschmal_23-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-hisschmal-23">
         [23]
        </a>
       </sup>
       This action followed previous protests in the state in opposition to neoliberal economic policies.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kovic_63-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-kovic-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Although it has been estimated
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2016)">
           by whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       as having no more than 300 armed guerrilla members, the EZLN paralyzed the Mexican government, which balked at the political risks of direct confrontation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296_61-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The major reason for this was that the rebellion caught the attention of the national and world press, as Marcos made full use of the then-new Internet to get the group's message out, putting the spotlight on indigenous issues in Mexico in general. Furthermore, the opposition press in Mexico City, especially
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/La_Jornada" title="La Jornada">
         La Jornada
        </a>
       </i>
       , actively supported the rebels. These factors encouraged the rebellion to go national.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296297_64-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296297-64">
         [64]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Many
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="This term requires quantification. (November 2016)">
           quantify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       blamed the unrest on infiltration of leftists among the large Central American refugee population in Chiapas,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia55_65-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia55-65">
         [65]
        </a>
       </sup>
       and the rebellion opened up splits in the countryside between those supporting and opposing the EZLN.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296_61-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Zapatista sympathizers have included mostly Protestants and
       <a href="/wiki/Word_of_God_(community)" title="Word of God (community)">
        Word of God
       </a>
       Catholics, opposing those "traditionalist" Catholics who practiced a syncretic form of Catholicism and indigenous beliefs. This split had existed in Chiapas since the 1970s, with the latter group supported by the
       <a href="/wiki/Cacique" title="Cacique">
        caciques
       </a>
       and others in the traditional power-structure. Protestants and Word of God Catholics (allied directly with the
       <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Diocese_of_San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_Las_Casas" title="Roman Catholic Diocese of San Cristóbal de Las Casas">
        bishopric in San Cristóbal
       </a>
       ) tended to oppose traditional power structures.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-kovic_63-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-kovic-63">
         [63]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Bishop of Chiapas,
       <a href="/wiki/Samuel_Ruiz" title="Samuel Ruiz">
        Samuel Ruiz
       </a>
       , and the Diocese of Chiapas reacted by offering to mediate between the rebels and authorities. However, because of this diocese's activism since the 1960s, authorities
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words">
          <span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (November 2016)">
           which?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       accused the clergy of being involved with the rebels.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mhidalgo112_66-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mhidalgo112-66">
         [66]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There was some ambiguity about the relationship between Ruiz and Marcos and it was a constant feature of news coverage, with many in official circles using such to discredit Ruiz. Eventually, the activities of the Zapatistas began to worry the Roman Catholic Church in general and to upstage the diocese's attempts to re establish itself among Chiapan indigenous communities against Protestant evangelization. This would lead to a breach between the Church and the Zapatistas.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296298_67-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296298-67">
         [67]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Zapatista story remained in headlines for a number
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers">
          <span title="This term requires quantification. (November 2016)">
           quantify
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       of years. One reason for this was the December 1997 massacre of forty-five Tzotzil peasants, mostly women and children in the Zapatista-controlled village of
       <a href="/wiki/Acteal" title="Acteal">
        Acteal
       </a>
       in the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chenhal%C3%B3&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chenhaló (page does not exist)">
        Chenhaló
       </a>
       municipality just north of San Cristóbal. This allowed many media outlets in Mexico to step up their criticisms of the government. However, the massacre was not carried out by the government but by civilians, demonstrating how the emergence of the Zapatista movement had divided indigenous groups.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett299300_68-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett299300-68">
         [68]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Despite this, the armed conflict was brief, mostly because the Zapatistas, unlike many other guerilla movements, did not try to gain traditional political power. It focussed more on trying to manipulate public opinion in order to obtain concessions from the government. This has linked the Zapatistas to other indigenous and
       <a href="/wiki/Identity_politics" title="Identity politics">
        identity-politics
       </a>
       movements that arose in the late-20th century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mhidalgo113_69-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mhidalgo113-69">
         [69]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main concession that the group received was the
       <a href="/wiki/San_Andr%C3%A9s_Accords" title="San Andrés Accords">
        San Andrés Accords
       </a>
       (1996), also known as the Law on Indian Rights and Culture.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-jrodriguez_24-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-jrodriguez-24">
         [24]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Accords appear to grant certain indigenous zones autonomy, but this is against the
       <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Mexico" title="Constitution of Mexico">
        Mexican constitution
       </a>
       ,
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       so its legitimacy has been questioned. Zapatista declarations since the mid-1990s have called for a new constitution.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett21_70-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett21-70">
         [70]
        </a>
       </sup>
       As of 1999
       <sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;">
        <a class="external text" href="//en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit">
         [update]
        </a>
       </sup>
       the government had not found a solution to this problem.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296_61-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The revolt also pressed the government to institute anti-poverty programs such as "Progresa" (later called "Oportunidades") and the "Puebla-Panama Plan" - aiming to increase trade between southern Mexico and Central America.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adultwomen_71-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-adultwomen-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       As of the first decade of the 2000s the Zapatista movement remained popular in many indigenous communities.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-adultwomen_71-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-adultwomen-71">
         [71]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The uprising gave indigenous peoples a more active role in the state's politics.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchis_18-31">
        <a href="#cite_note-enchis-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       However, it did not solve the economic issues that many peasant farmers face, especially the lack of land to cultivate. This problem has been at crisis proportions since the 1970s, and the government's reaction has been to encourage peasant farmers—mostly indigenous—to migrate into the sparsely populated Lacandon Jungle, a trend since earlier in the century.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296_61-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       From the 1970s on, some 100,000 people set up homes in this rainforest area, with many being recognized as
       <i>
        ejidos
       </i>
       , or communal land-holding organizations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hamnett296_61-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-Hamnett296-61">
         [61]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These migrants included Tzeltals, Tojolabals, Ch'ols and mestizos, mostly farming corn and beans and raising livestock. However, the government changed policies in the late 1980s with the establishment of the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montes_Azules_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Montes Azules Biosphere Reserve">
        Montes Azules Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       , as much of the Lacandon Jungle had been destroyed or severely damaged.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevenson_72-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-stevenson-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       While armed resistance has wound down, the Zapatistas have remained a strong political force, especially around San Cristóbal and the Lacandon Jungle, its traditional bases. Since the Accords, they have shifted focus in gaining autonomy for the communities they control.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historycom_22-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-historycom-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73">
        <a href="#cite_note-73">
         [73]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Since the 1994 uprising, migration into the Lacandon Jungle has significantly increased, involving illegal settlements and cutting in the protected biosphere reserve. The Zapatistas support these actions as part of indigenous rights, but that has put them in conflict with international environmental groups and with the indigenous inhabitants of the rainforest area, the
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_people" title="Lacandon people">
        Lacandons
       </a>
       . Environmental groups state that the settlements pose grave risks to what remains of the Lacandon, while the Zapatistas accuse them of being fronts for the government, which wants to open the rainforest up to multinational corporations.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevenson_72-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-stevenson-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weinberg_74-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-weinberg-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Added to this is the possibility that significant oil and gas deposits exist under this area.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Zapatista movement has had some successes. The agricultural sector of the economy now favors
       <i>
        ejidos
       </i>
       and other commonly-owned land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-enchis_18-32">
        <a href="#cite_note-enchis-18">
         [18]
        </a>
       </sup>
       There have been some other gains economically as well. In the last decades of the 20th century, Chiapas's traditional agricultural economy has diversified somewhat with the construction of more roads and better infrastructure by the federal and state governments. Tourism has become important in some areas of the state, especially in San Cristóbal de las Casas and Palenque.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rincones34_75-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-rincones34-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Its economy is important to Mexico as a whole as well, producing coffee, corn, cacao, tobacco, sugar, fruit, vegetable and honey for export. It is also a key state for the nation's petrochemical and hydroelectric industries. A significant percentage of PEMEX's drilling and refining takes place in Chiapas and Tabasco, and Chiapas produces fifty-five percent of Mexico's hydroelectric energy.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mgarcia54_58-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-mgarcia54-58">
         [58]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       However, Chiapas remains one of the poorest states in Mexico. Ninety-four of its 111 municipalities have a large percentage of the population living in poverty. In areas such as Ocosingo, Altamirano and Las Margaritas, the towns where the Zapatistas first came into prominence in 1994, 48% of the adults are illiterate. Chiapas is still considered
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch">
          <span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (November 2016)">
           by whom?
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
       isolated and distant from the rest of Mexico, both culturally and geographically. It has significantly underdeveloped infrastructure compared to the rest of the country, and its significant indigenous population with isolationist tendencies keep the state distinct culturally.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-rincones34_75-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-rincones34-75">
         [75]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Cultural stratification, neglect and lack of investment by the Mexican federal government has exacerbated this problem.
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed">
          <span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2016)">
           citation needed
          </span>
         </a>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">
        Geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Political_geography">
        Political geography
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Political geography">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <p>
       Chiapas is located in the south east of Mexico, bordering the states of
       <a href="/wiki/Tabasco" title="Tabasco">
        Tabasco
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Veracruz" title="Veracruz">
        Veracruz
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Oaxaca" title="Oaxaca">
        Oaxaca
       </a>
       with the
       <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Ocean" title="Pacific Ocean">
        Pacific Ocean
       </a>
       to the south and
       <a href="/wiki/Guatemala" title="Guatemala">
        Guatemala
       </a>
       to the east. It has a territory of 74,415 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       , the eighth largest state in Mexico. The state consists of 118 municipalities organized into nine political regions called Center, Altos, Fronteriza, Frailesca, Norte, Selva, Sierra, Soconusco and Istmo-Costa. There are 18 cities, twelve towns (villas) and 111 pueblos (villages).
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pimienta_76-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-pimienta-76">
         [76]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ubicagob_77-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ubicagob-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Major cities include
       <a href="/wiki/Tuxtla_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Tuxtla Gutiérrez">
        Tuxtla Gutiérrez
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/San_Crist%C3%B3bal_de_las_Casas" title="San Cristóbal de las Casas">
        San Cristóbal de las Casas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tapachula" title="Tapachula">
        Tapachula
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Palenque,_Chiapas" title="Palenque, Chiapas">
        Palenque
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Comit%C3%A1n,_Chiapas" title="Comitán, Chiapas">
        Comitán
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Chiapa_de_Corzo,_Chiapas" title="Chiapa de Corzo, Chiapas">
        Chiapa de Corzo
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historycom_22-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-historycom-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ubicagob_77-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-ubicagob-77">
         [77]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Geographical_regions">
        Geographical regions
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Geographical regions">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg/220px-Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg/330px-Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/12/Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg/440px-Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Volcan_Tacana_01.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Mount Tacaná
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Sumideroclouds.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1200" data-file-width="1600" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sumideroclouds.jpg/220px-Sumideroclouds.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sumideroclouds.jpg/330px-Sumideroclouds.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a6/Sumideroclouds.jpg/440px-Sumideroclouds.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Sumideroclouds.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the Sumidero Canyon from atop of the ridge
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Montebello_02.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="768" data-file-width="1024" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Montebello_02.jpg/220px-Montebello_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Montebello_02.jpg/330px-Montebello_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/99/Montebello_02.jpg/440px-Montebello_02.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Montebello_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Lake at the Parque Nacional Lagunas de Montebello
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The state has a complex geography with seven distinct regions according to the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Mullerried_classification_system&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Mullerried classification system (page does not exist)">
        Mullerried classification system
       </a>
       . These include the Pacific Coast Plains, the Sierra Madre de Chiapas, the Central Depression, the Central Highlands, the Eastern Mountains, the Northern Mountains and the Gulf Coast Plains. The Pacific Coast Plains is a strip of land parallel to the ocean. It is composed mostly of sediment from the mountains that border it on the northern side. It is uniformly flat, and stretches from the Bernal Mountain south to
       <a href="/wiki/Tonal%C3%A1,_Chiapas" title="Tonalá, Chiapas">
        Tonalá
       </a>
       . It has deep salty soils due to its proximity to the sea. It has mostly deciduous rainforest although most has been converted to pasture for cattle and fields for crops. It has numerous
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">
        estuaries
       </a>
       with
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Mangroves" title="Mangroves">
        mangroves
       </a>
       and other aquatic vegetation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">
        Sierra Madre de Chiapas
       </a>
       runs parallel to the Pacific coastline of the state, northwest to southeast as a continuation of the
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_del_Sur" title="Sierra Madre del Sur">
        Sierra Madre del Sur
       </a>
       . This area has the highest altitudes in Chiapas including the
       <a href="/wiki/Volc%C3%A1n_Tacan%C3%A1" title="Volcán Tacaná">
        Tacaná Volcano
       </a>
       , which rises 4,093 m (13,428 ft) above sea level. Most of these mountains are volcanic in origin although the nucleus is metamorphic rock. It has a wide range of climates but little arable land. It is mostly covered in middle altitude rainforest, high altitude rainforest, and forests of oaks and pines.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The mountains partially block rain clouds from the Pacific, a process known as
       <a href="/wiki/Orographic_lift" title="Orographic lift">
        Orographic lift
       </a>
       , which creates a particularly rich coastal region called the
       <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">
        Soconusco
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CFE_79-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-CFE-79">
         [79]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The main commercial center of the sierra is the town of
       <a href="/wiki/Motozintla" title="Motozintla">
        Motozintla
       </a>
       , also near the Guatemalan border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Central Depression is in the center of the state. It is an extensive semi flat area bordered by the Sierra Madre de Chiapas, the Central Highlands and the Northern Mountains. Within the depression there are a number of distinct valleys. The climate here can be very hot and humid in the summer, especially due to the large volume of rain received in July and August. The original vegetation was lowland deciduous rainforest with some rainforest of middle altitudes and some oaks above 1,500 metres (4,900 ft) above sea level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Central Highlands, also referred to as Los Altos, are mountains oriented from northwest to southeast with altitudes ranging from twelve to sixteen hundred meters above sea level. The western highlands are displaced faults, while the eastern highlands are mainly folds of sedimentary formations – mainly
       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">
        limestone
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Shale" title="Shale">
        shale
       </a>
       , and
       <a href="/wiki/Sandstone" title="Sandstone">
        sandstone
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       These mountains, along the Sierra Madre of Chiapas become the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Cuchumatanes" title="Cuchumatanes">
        Cuchumatanes
       </a>
       where they extend over the border into Guatemala. Its topography is mountainous with many narrow valleys and
       <a href="/wiki/Karst" title="Karst">
        karst
       </a>
       formations called
       <a href="/wiki/Uvala_(landform)" title="Uvala (landform)">
        uvalas
       </a>
       or poljés, depending on the size. Most of the rock is
       <a href="/wiki/Limestone" title="Limestone">
        limestone
       </a>
       allowing for a number of formations such as caves and sinkholes. There are also some isolated pockets of volcanic rock with the tallest peaks being the
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Tzontehuitz&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Tzontehuitz (page does not exist)">
        Tzontehuitz
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Huitepec" title="Huitepec">
        Huitepec
       </a>
       volcanos. There are no significant surface water systems as they are almost all underground. The original vegetation was forest of oak and pine but these have been heavily damaged.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The highlands climate in the
       <a href="/wiki/K%C3%B6ppen_climate_classification" title="Köppen climate classification">
        Koeppen modified classification
       </a>
       system for Mexico is humid temperate C(m) and subhumid temperate C (w 2 ) (w). This climate exhibits a summer rainy season and a dry winter, with possibilities of frost from December to March.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Central Highlands have been the population center of Chiapas since the
       <a href="/wiki/Spanish_conquest_of_the_Aztec_Empire" title="Spanish conquest of the Aztec Empire">
        Conquest
       </a>
       . European
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Epidemics" title="Epidemics">
        epidemics
       </a>
       were hindered by the
       <a href="/wiki/Tierra_fr%C3%ADa" title="Tierra fría">
        tierra fría
       </a>
       climate, allowing the indigenous peoples in the highlands to retain their large numbers.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ben1_80-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-ben1-80">
         [80]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Eastern Mountains (Montañas del Oriente) are in the east of the state, formed by various parallel mountain chains mostly made of limestone and sandstone. Its altitude varies from 500 to 1,500 m (1,600 to 4,900 ft). This area receives moisture from the
       <a href="/wiki/Gulf_of_Mexico" title="Gulf of Mexico">
        Gulf of Mexico
       </a>
       with abundant rainfall and exuberant vegetation, which creates the
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_Jungle" title="Lacandon Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </a>
       , one of the most important rainforests in Mexico. The Northern Mountains (Montañas del Norte) are in the north of the state. They separate the flatlands of the Gulf Coast Plains from the Central Depression. Its rock is mostly limestone. These mountains also receive large amounts of rainfall with moisture from the Gulf of Mexico giving it a mostly hot and humid climate with rains year round. In the highest elevations around 1,800 m (5,900 ft), temperatures are somewhat cooler and do experience a winter. The terrain is rugged with small valleys whose natural vegetation is high altitude rainforest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-4">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The Gulf Coast Plains (Llanura Costera del Golfo) stretch into Chiapas from the state of Tabasco, which gives it the alternate name of the Tabasqueña Plains. These plains are found only in the extreme north of the state. The terrain is flat and prone to flooding during the rainy season as it was built by sediments deposited by rivers and streams heading to the Gulf.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Lacandon_Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Lacandon Jungle">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GroupCPalenque11.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/GroupCPalenque11.JPG/220px-GroupCPalenque11.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/GroupCPalenque11.JPG/330px-GroupCPalenque11.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4b/GroupCPalenque11.JPG/440px-GroupCPalenque11.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GroupCPalenque11.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Jungle area near Group C at the Palenque archeological site
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">
       Main article:
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_Jungle" title="Lacandon Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </a>
      </div>
      <p>
       The Lacandon Jungle is situated in north eastern Chiapas, centered on a series of canyonlike valleys called the Cañadas, between smaller mountain ridges oriented from northwest to southeast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manejo_81-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-manejo-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The ecosystem covers an area of approximately 1.9 million hectares extending from Chiapas into northern Guatemala and southern
       <a href="/wiki/Yucat%C3%A1n_Peninsula" title="Yucatán Peninsula">
        Yucatán Peninsula
       </a>
       and into
       <a href="/wiki/Belize" title="Belize">
        Belize
       </a>
       . This area contains as much as 25% of Mexico's total species diversity,
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-cheng_82-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-cheng-82">
         [82]
        </a>
       </sup>
       most of which has not been researched.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abianco_83-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-abianco-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It has a predominantly hot and humid climate (Am w" i g) with most rain falling from summer to part of fall, with an average of between 2300 and 2600 mm per year. There is a short dry season from March to May. The predominate wild vegetation is perennial high rainforest.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-manejo_81-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-manejo-81">
         [81]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Lacandon comprises a biosphere reserve (Montes Azules); four natural protected areas (
       <a href="/wiki/Bonampak" title="Bonampak">
        Bonampak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Yaxchilan" title="Yaxchilan">
        Yaxchilan
       </a>
       , Chan Kin, and Lacantum); and the communal reserve (La Cojolita), which functions as a biological corridor with the area of
       <a href="/wiki/Pet%C3%A9n_Basin" title="Petén Basin">
        Petén
       </a>
       in Guatemala. Flowing within the Rainforest is the
       <a href="/wiki/Usumacinta_River" title="Usumacinta River">
        Usumacinta River
       </a>
       , considered to be one of the largest rivers in Mexico and seventh largest in the world based on volume of water.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wwf_84-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-wwf-84">
         [84]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">
        [
        <i>
         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Accuracy_dispute#Disputed_statement" title="Wikipedia:Accuracy dispute">
          <span title="The material near this tag is possibly inaccurate or nonfactual. (March 2014)">
           dubious
          </span>
         </a>
         <span class="metadata">
          –
          <a href="/wiki/Talk:Chiapas#Dubious" title="Talk:Chiapas">
           discuss
          </a>
         </span>
        </i>
        ]
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="480" data-file-width="720" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg/220px-Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg/330px-Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/45/Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg/440px-Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Laguna_Miramar_en_la_Selva_Lacandona.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Miramar Lake surrounded by the Lacandon Jungle
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       During the 20th century, the Lacandon has had a dramatic increase in population and along with it, severe
       <a href="/wiki/Deforestation" title="Deforestation">
        deforestation
       </a>
       . The population of municipalities in this area,
       <a href="/wiki/Altamirano,_Chiapas" title="Altamirano, Chiapas">
        Altamirano
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Margaritas,_Chiapas" title="Las Margaritas, Chiapas">
        Las Margaritas
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ocosingo" title="Ocosingo">
        Ocosingo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Palenque,_Chiapas" title="Palenque, Chiapas">
        Palenque
       </a>
       have risen from 11,000 in 1920 to over 376,000 in 2000.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mhidalgo106_49-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-mhidalgo106-49">
         [49]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Migrants include
       <a href="/wiki/Ch%27ol_people" title="Ch'ol people">
        Ch'ol
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tzeltal" title="Tzeltal">
        Tzeltal
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Tzotzil_people" title="Tzotzil people">
        Tzotzil
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Tojolabal" title="Tojolabal">
        Tojolabal
       </a>
       indigenous peoples along with mestizos, Guatemalan refugees and others.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_85-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Most of these migrants are peasant farmers, who cut forest to plant crops. However, the soil of this area cannot support annual crop farming for more than three or four harvents.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The increase in population and the need to move on to new lands has pitted migrants against each other, the native Lacandon people, and the various ecological reserves for land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevenson_72-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-stevenson-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weinberg_74-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-weinberg-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-washingtonpost.com_85-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-washingtonpost.com-85">
         [85]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is estimated that only ten percent of the original Lacandon rainforest in Mexico remains, with the rest strip-mined, logged and farmed. It once stretched over a large part of eastern Chiapas but all that remains is along the northern edge of the Guatemalan border.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mbidiuk_86-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-mbidiuk-86">
         [86]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Of this remaining portion, Mexico is losing over five percent each year.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-diemont_87-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-diemont-87">
         [87]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The best preserved portion of the Lacandon is within the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Montes_Azules_Biosphere_Reserve" title="Montes Azules Biosphere Reserve">
        Montes Azules Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zonasarq_88-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-zonasarq-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is centered on what was a commercial logging grant by the
       <a href="/wiki/Porfirio_D%C3%ADaz" title="Porfirio Díaz">
        Porfirio Díaz
       </a>
       government, which the government later nationalized. However, this nationalization and conversion into a reserve has made it one of the most contested lands in Chiapas, with the already existing ejidos and other settlements within the park along with new arrivals squatting on the land.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-stevenson_72-3">
        <a href="#cite_note-stevenson-72">
         [72]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h3>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Soconusco">
        Soconusco
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Soconusco">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h3>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:PastureSierraChiapas.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/PastureSierraChiapas.JPG/220px-PastureSierraChiapas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/PastureSierraChiapas.JPG/330px-PastureSierraChiapas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/1/1d/PastureSierraChiapas.JPG/440px-PastureSierraChiapas.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:PastureSierraChiapas.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of Sierra Madre de Chiapas from the Soconusco Region
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">
        Soconusco
       </a>
       region encompasses a coastal plain and a mountain range with elevations of up to 2000 meters above sea levels paralleling the Pacific Coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atoussaint_89-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-atoussaint-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The highest peak in Chiapas is the
       <a href="/wiki/Volc%C3%A1n_Tacan%C3%A1" title="Volcán Tacaná">
        Tacaná Volcano
       </a>
       at 4,800 meters above sea level.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zonainflu_90-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-zonainflu-90">
         [90]
        </a>
       </sup>
       In accordance with an 1882 treaty, the dividing line between Mexico and Guatemala goes right over the summit of this volcano.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-abianco_83-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-abianco-83">
         [83]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The climate is tropical, with a number of rivers and evergreen forests in the mountains. This is Chiapas’ major coffee producing area, as it has the best soils and climate for coffee.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Before the arrival of the Spanish, this area was the principal source of
       <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">
        cocoa
       </a>
       seeds in the Aztec empire, which they used as currency, and for the highly prized
       <a href="/wiki/Quetzal" title="Quetzal">
        quetzal
       </a>
       feathers used by the nobility. It would become the first area to produce coffee, introduced by an Italian entrepreneur on the La Chacara farm.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-martineztorres_34-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-martineztorres-34">
         [34]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Coffee is cultivated on the slopes of these mountains mostly between 600 and 1200 masl. Mexico produces about 4 million sacks of green coffee each year, fifth in the world behind
       <a href="/wiki/Brazil" title="Brazil">
        Brazil
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Colombia" title="Colombia">
        Colombia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Indonesia" title="Indonesia">
        Indonesia
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Vietnam" title="Vietnam">
        Vietnam
       </a>
       . Most producers are small with plots of land under five hectares. From November to January, the annual crop is harvested and processed employing thousands of seasonal workers. Lately, a number of coffee haciendas have been developing tourism infrastructure as well.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-atoussaint_89-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-atoussaint-89">
         [89]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <h2>
       <span class="mw-headline" id="Environment_and_protected_areas">
        Environment and protected areas
       </span>
       <span class="mw-editsection">
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         [
        </span>
        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapas&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Environment and protected areas">
         edit
        </a>
        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">
         ]
        </span>
       </span>
      </h2>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1944" data-file-width="2592" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG/220px-Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG/330px-Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/a/a2/Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG/440px-Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Agua_azul_Chiapas.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         View of the waterfalls at Agua Azul
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2547" data-file-width="3872" height="145" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG/220px-UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG/330px-UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b7/UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG/440px-UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:UsumacintaYaxchilan16.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Usumacinta River and Lacandon Jungle on Chiapas side
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg/220px-GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg/330px-GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/ff/GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg/440px-GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:GrijalvaRiverCorzo.jpg" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Grijalva River flowing through the central region
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       Chiapas is located in the tropical belt of the planet, but the climate is moderated in many areas by altitude. For this reason, there are hot, semi-hot, temperate and even cold climates. Some areas have abundant rainfall year-round and others receive most of their rain between May and October, with a dry season from November to April. The mountain areas affect wind and moisture flow over the state, concentrating moisture in certain areas of the state. They also are responsible for some cloud-covered rainforest areas in the
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">
        Sierra Madre
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Chiapas' rainforests are home to thousands of animals and plants, some of which cannot be found anywhere else in the world.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historycom_22-5">
        <a href="#cite_note-historycom-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Natural vegetation varies from lowland to highland tropical forest, pine and oak forests in the highest altitudes and plains area with some grassland. Chiapas is ranked second in forest resources in Mexico with valued woods such as pine,
       <a href="/wiki/Cypress" title="Cypress">
        cypress
       </a>
       ,
       <i>
        <a href="/wiki/Liquidambar" title="Liquidambar">
         Liquidambar
        </a>
       </i>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Oak" title="Oak">
        oak
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cedar_wood" title="Cedar wood">
        cedar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mahogany" title="Mahogany">
        mahogany
       </a>
       and more. The
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_Jungle" title="Lacandon Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </a>
       is one of the last major tropical rainforests in the northern hemisphere with an extension of 600,000 hectares (1,500,000 acres). It contains about sixty percent of Mexico’s tropical tree species, 3,500 species of plants, 1,157 species of invertebrates and over 500 of vertebrate species. Chiapas has one of the greatest diversities in wildlife in the Americas. There are more than 100 species of amphibians, 700 species of birds, fifty of mammals and just over 200 species of reptiles. In the hot lowlands, there are
       <a href="/wiki/Armadillo" title="Armadillo">
        armadillos
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Monkey" title="Monkey">
        monkeys
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pelican" title="Pelican">
        pelicans
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Wild_boar" title="Wild boar">
        wild boar
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Jaguar" title="Jaguar">
        jaguars
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Crocodile" title="Crocodile">
        crocodiles
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Iguana" title="Iguana">
        iguanas
       </a>
       and many others. In the temperate regions there are species such as
       <a href="/wiki/Bobcat" title="Bobcat">
        bobcats
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Salamander" title="Salamander">
        salamanders
       </a>
       , a large red lizard
       <a href="/wiki/Abronia_lythrochila" title="Abronia lythrochila">
        Abronia lythrochila
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Weasel" title="Weasel">
        weasels
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Opossum" title="Opossum">
        opossums
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Deer" title="Deer">
        deer
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ocelot" title="Ocelot">
        ocelots
       </a>
       and bats. The coastal areas have large quantities of fish, turtles, and
       <a href="/wiki/Crustacean" title="Crustacean">
        crustaceans
       </a>
       , with many species in danger of extinction or endangered as they are endemic only to this area. The total biodiversity of the state is estimated at over 50,000 species of plants and animals. The diversity of species is not limited to the hot lowlands. The higher altitudes also have
       <a href="/wiki/Mesophile" title="Mesophile">
        mesophile
       </a>
       forests, oak/pine forests in the Los Altos, Northern Mountains and Sierra Madre and the extensive
       <a href="/wiki/Estuary" title="Estuary">
        estuaries
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Mangrove" title="Mangrove">
        mangrove
       </a>
       wetlands along the coast.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       Chiapas has about thirty percent of Mexico’s fresh water resources. The Sierra Madre divides them into those that flow to the Pacific and those that flow to the Gulf of Mexico. Most of the first are short rivers and streams; most longer ones flow to the Gulf. Most Pacific side rivers do not drain directly into this ocean but into
       <a href="/wiki/Lagoon" title="Lagoon">
        lagoons
       </a>
       and estuaries. The two largest rivers are the
       <a href="/wiki/Grijalva_River" title="Grijalva River">
        Grijalva
       </a>
       and the
       <a href="/wiki/Usumacinta_River" title="Usumacinta River">
        Usumacinta
       </a>
       , with both part of the same system. The Grijalva has four dams built on it the Belisario Dominguez (La Angostura); Manuel Moreno Torres (Chicoasén); Nezahualcóyotl (Malpaso); and Angel Albino Corzo (Peñitas). The Usumacinta divides the state from Guatemala and is the longest river in
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       . In total, the state has 110,000 hectares (270,000 acres) of surface waters, 260 km (160 mi) of coastline, control of 96,000 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (37,000 sq mi) of ocean, 75,230 hectares (185,900 acres) of estuaries and ten lake systems.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-8">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Laguna Miramar is a lake in the Montes Azules reserve and the largest in the Lacandon Jungle at 40 km in diameter. The color of its waters varies from
       <a href="/wiki/Indigo" title="Indigo">
        indigo
       </a>
       to
       <a href="/wiki/Emerald" title="Emerald">
        emerald
       </a>
       green and in ancient times, there were settlements on its islands and its caves on the shoreline. The Catazajá Lake is 28 km north of the city of
       <a href="/wiki/Palenque,_Chiapas" title="Palenque, Chiapas">
        Palenque
       </a>
       . It is formed by rainwater captured as it makes it way to the Usumacinta River. It contains wildlife such as
       <a href="/wiki/Manatee" title="Manatee">
        manatees
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Iguana" title="Iguana">
        iguanas
       </a>
       and it is surrounded by rainforest. Fishing on this lake is an ancient tradition and the lake has an annual bass fishing tournament. The Welib Já Waterfall is located on the road between Palenque and Bonampak.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-zonasarq_88-1">
        <a href="#cite_note-zonasarq-88">
         [88]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:MalpasoDam02.JPG">
         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MalpasoDam02.JPG/220px-MalpasoDam02.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MalpasoDam02.JPG/330px-MalpasoDam02.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/MalpasoDam02.JPG/440px-MalpasoDam02.JPG 2x" width="220"/>
        </a>
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:MalpasoDam02.JPG" title="Enlarge">
          </a>
         </div>
         Overlooking part of the Malpaso or Nezahualcoyotl Reservoir
        </div>
       </div>
      </div>
      <p>
       The state has thirty-six protected areas at the state and federal levels along with 67 areas protected by various municipalities. The
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Sumidero_Canyon_National_Park" title="Sumidero Canyon National Park">
        Sumidero Canyon National Park
       </a>
       was decreed in 1980 with an extension of 21,789 hectares (53,840 acres). It extends over two of the regions of the state, the Central Depression and the Central Highlands over the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Tuxtla_Guti%C3%A9rrez" title="Tuxtla Gutiérrez">
        Tuxtla Gutiérrez
       </a>
       ,
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Nuevo_Usumacinta&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Nuevo Usumacinta (page does not exist)">
        Nuevo Usumacinta
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Chiapa_de_Corzo,_Chiapas" title="Chiapa de Corzo, Chiapas">
        Chiapa de Corzo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/San_Fernando,_Chiapas" title="San Fernando, Chiapas">
        San Fernando
       </a>
       . The
       <a href="/wiki/Sumidero_Canyon" title="Sumidero Canyon">
        canyon
       </a>
       has steep and vertical sides that rise to up to 1000 meters from the river below with mostly tropical rainforest but some areas with
       <a href="/wiki/Xerophile" title="Xerophile">
        xerophile
       </a>
       vegetation such as cactus can be found. The river below, which has cut the canyon over the course of twelve million years, is called the
       <a href="/wiki/Grijalva_River" title="Grijalva River">
        Grijalva
       </a>
       . The canyon is emblematic for the state as it is featured in the state seal.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-9">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-canoninsolito_91-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-canoninsolito-91">
         [91]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The Sumidero Canyon was once the site of a battle between the Spaniards and
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Chiapanecan&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Chiapanecan (page does not exist)">
        Chiapanecan
       </a>
       Indians. Many Chiapanecans chose to throw themselves from the high edges of the canyon rather than be defeated by Spanish forces. Today, the canyon is a popular destination for
       <a href="/wiki/Ecotourism" title="Ecotourism">
        ecotourism
       </a>
       . Visitors often take boat trips down the river that runs through the canyon and enjoy the area's natural beauty including the many birds and abundant vegetation.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historycom_22-6">
        <a href="#cite_note-historycom-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Montes_Azules_Integral_Biosphere_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Montes Azules Integral Biosphere Reserve (page does not exist)">
        Montes Azules Integral Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       was decreed in 1978. It is located in the northeast of the state in the
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_Jungle" title="Lacandon Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </a>
       . It covers 331,200 hectares (818,000 acres) in the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Maravilla_Tenejapa" title="Maravilla Tenejapa">
        Maravilla Tenejapa
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Ocosingo" title="Ocosingo">
        Ocosingo
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Las_Margaritas,_Chiapas" title="Las Margaritas, Chiapas">
        Las Margaritas
       </a>
       . It conserves highland perennial rainforest. The jungle is in the Usumacinta River basin east of the Chiapas Highlands. It is recognized by the
       <a href="/wiki/United_Nations_Environment_Programme" title="United Nations Environment Programme">
        United Nations Environment Programme
       </a>
       for its global biological and cultural significance. In 1992, the 61,874-hectare (152,890-acre) Lacantun Reserve, which includes the Classic Maya archaeological sites of
       <a href="/wiki/Yaxchilan" title="Yaxchilan">
        Yaxchilan
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Bonampak" title="Bonampak">
        Bonampak
       </a>
       , was added to the biosphere reserve.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-weinberg_74-2">
        <a href="#cite_note-weinberg-74">
         [74]
        </a>
       </sup>
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-10">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       <a href="/wiki/Agua_Azul" title="Agua Azul">
        Agua Azul Waterfall Protection Area
       </a>
       is in the Northern Mountains in the municipality of
       <a href="/wiki/Tumbal%C3%A1" title="Tumbalá">
        Tumbalá
       </a>
       . It covers an area of 2,580 hectares (6,400 acres) of rainforest and pine-oak forest, centered on the waterfalls it is named after.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-11">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is located in an area locally called the "Mountains of Water", as many rivers flow through there on their way to the Gulf of Mexico. The rugged terrain encourages waterfalls with large pools at the bottom, that the falling water has carved into the sedimentary rock and limestone. Agua Azul is one of the best known in the state. The waters of the Agua Azul River emerge from a cave that forms a natural bridge of thirty meters and five small waterfalls in succession, all with pools of water at the bottom. In addition to Agua Azul, the area has other attractions—such as the Shumuljá River, which contains rapids and waterfalls, the
       <a href="/wiki/Misol_H%C3%A1" title="Misol Há">
        Misol Há
       </a>
       Waterfall with a thirty-meter drop, the Bolón Ajau Waterfall with a fourteen-meter drop, the Gallito Copetón rapids, the Blacquiazules Waterfalls, and a section of calm water called the Agua Clara.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-azulinsolito_92-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-azulinsolito-92">
         [92]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <p>
       The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Ocote_Biosphere_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Ocote Biosphere Reserve (page does not exist)">
        El Ocote Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       was decreed in 1982 located in the Northern Mountains at the boundary with the Sierra Madre del Sur in the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/Ocozocoautla_de_Espinosa" title="Ocozocoautla de Espinosa">
        Ocozocoautla
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Cintalapa" title="Cintalapa">
        Cintalapa
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Tecpat%C3%A1n" title="Tecpatán">
        Tecpatán
       </a>
       . It has a surface area of 101,288.15 hectares (250,288.5 acres) and preserves a rainforest area with karst formations. The
       <a href="/wiki/Lagunas_de_Montebello_National_Park" title="Lagunas de Montebello National Park">
        Lagunas de Montebello National Park
       </a>
       was decreed in 1959 and consists of 7,371 hectares (18,210 acres) near the Guatemalan border in the municipalities of
       <a href="/wiki/La_Independencia,_Chiapas" title="La Independencia, Chiapas">
        La Independencia
       </a>
       and
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/La_Trinitaria,_Mexico" title="La Trinitaria, Mexico">
        La Trinitaria
       </a>
       . It contains two of the most threatened ecosystems in Mexico the "cloud rainforest" and the
       <a href="/wiki/Soconusco" title="Soconusco">
        Soconusco
       </a>
       rainforest. The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=El_Triunfo_Biosphere_Reserve&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="El Triunfo Biosphere Reserve (page does not exist)">
        El Triunfo Biosphere Reserve
       </a>
       , decreed in 1990, is located in the
       <a href="/wiki/Sierra_Madre_de_Chiapas" title="Sierra Madre de Chiapas">
        Sierra Madre de Chiapas
       </a>
       in the municipalities of
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Acacoyagua" title="Acacoyagua">
        Acacoyagua
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/%C3%81ngel_Albino_Corzo" title="Ángel Albino Corzo">
        Ángel Albino Corzo
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Montecristo_de_Guerrero" title="Montecristo de Guerrero">
        Montecristo de Guerrero
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/La_Concordia,_Chiapas" title="La Concordia, Chiapas">
        La Concordia
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Mapastepec" title="Mapastepec">
        Mapastepec
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Pijijiapan" title="Pijijiapan">
        Pijijiapan
       </a>
       ,
       <a href="/wiki/Siltepec" title="Siltepec">
        Siltepec
       </a>
       and
       <a href="/wiki/Villa_Corzo" title="Villa Corzo">
        Villa Corzo
       </a>
       near the Pacific Ocean with 119,177.29 hectares (294,493.5 acres). It conserves areas of tropical rainforest and many freshwater systems endemic to
       <a href="/wiki/Central_America" title="Central America">
        Central America
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-12">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       It is home to around 400 species of birds including several rare species such as the
       <a href="/wiki/Horned_guan" title="Horned guan">
        horned guan
       </a>
       , the
       <a href="/wiki/Quetzal" title="Quetzal">
        quetzal
       </a>
       and the
       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Azure-rumped_tanager" title="Azure-rumped tanager">
        azure-rumped tanager
       </a>
       .
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-historycom_22-7">
        <a href="#cite_note-historycom-22">
         [22]
        </a>
       </sup>
       The
       <a href="/wiki/Palenque" title="Palenque">
        Palenque National Forest
       </a>
       is centered on the archaeological site of the same name and was decreed in 1981. It is located in the municipality of Palenque where the Northern Mountains meet the Gulf Coast Plain. It extends over 1,381 hectares (3,410 acres) of tropical rainforest. The
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Laguna_B%C3%A9lgica_Conservation_Zone&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Laguna Bélgica Conservation Zone (page does not exist)">
        Laguna Bélgica Conservation Zone
       </a>
       is located in the north west of the state in the municipality of Ocozocoautla. It covers forty-two hectares centered on the Bélgica Lake. The El
       <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=Zapotal_Ecological_Center&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Zapotal Ecological Center (page does not exist)">
        Zapotal Ecological Center
       </a>
       was established in 1980.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mediofisico_78-13">
        <a href="#cite_note-mediofisico-78">
         [78]
        </a>
       </sup>
       Nahá – Metzabok is an area in the
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_Jungle" title="Lacandon Jungle">
        Lacandon Jungle
       </a>
       whose name means "place of the black lord" in
       <a href="/wiki/Nahuatl" title="Nahuatl">
        Nahuatl
       </a>
       . It extends over 617.49 km
       <sup>
        2
       </sup>
       (238.41 sq mi) and in 2010, it was included in the
       <a href="/wiki/World_Network_of_Biosphere_Reserves" title="World Network of Biosphere Reserves">
        World Network of Biosphere Reserves
       </a>
       . Two main communities in the area are called Nahá and Metzabok. They were established in the 1940s, but the oldest communities in the area belong to the
       <a href="/wiki/Lacandon_people" title="Lacandon people">
        Lacandon people
       </a>
       . The area has large numbers of wildlife including endangered species such as eagles, quetzals and jaguars.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aventuragob_93-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-aventuragob-93">
         [93]
        </a>
       </sup>
      </p>
      <div align="center">

        <tr>
         <td align="center" bgcolor="white" valign="center">

      <p>
       As of 2010, the population is 4,796,580, the eighth most populous state in Mexico.
       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-inegipob_96-0">
        <a href="#cite_note-inegipob-96">
         [96]
        </a>
       </sup>
